doc_id=94.tetml page=48 block_id=48-8 bbox=67.4,281.8,545.5,451.0 1017 1024
line=1017  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:       The other school of thought (which we can call the case movement family of theories) rejects this
line=1018  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :conclusion. In particular, it abandons the view that the phrasal movement which resolves ACD in a direct
line=1019  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :object is limited to particular subtypes of DPs. According to this proposal, developed independently by
line=1020  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :Lasnik (1993) and by Hornstein (1994; 1995), the covert phrasal movement that licenses ACD is not limited
line=1021  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :to "special DPs", but is actually a much more "garden-variety" type of movement — namely, movement for
line=1022  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :reasons of Case. Lasnik and Hornstein develop their proposals in the context of Chomsky's (1995, chapters
line=1023  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :2-3) proposal that object Case is checked — not within VP — but in a VP-external projection (AGRoP in
line=1024  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:Chomsky 1995, chapter 1; vP in Chomsky 1995, chapter 4) to which the object moves. They suggest that it

doc_id=94.tetml page=48 block_id=48-9 bbox=67.4,74.4,544.6,268.8 1025 1033
line=1025  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :is this kind of Case-driven movement, not QR or covert wh-movement, that resolves ACD in the standard
line=1026  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51 :cases.33 They develop this proposal as part of a broader proposal that QR does not exist, which I will not
line=1027  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51 :report here.34
line=1028  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       The central difference between the "limited movement" and the "case movement" approaches lies in
line=1029  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :whether ACD resolution within direct objects is brought about by special processes that are limited to certain
line=1030  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :DP-types (quantified phrases and wh-phrases), or whether ACD resolution is available to all direct object
line=1031  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :DPs that bear object Case. Some of the arguments developed by Kennedy (1997) help answer this question,
line=1032  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:by arguing for the weak point that covert operations other than Case movement must at least be allowed to
line=1033  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :resolve ACD. As Kennedy notes, there are instances of ACD that require a type of movement that Case

doc_id=94.tetml page=56 block_id=56-5 bbox=100.9,598.0,533.6,611.0 1202 1202
line=1202  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:Except in questions where a wh-phrase is D-linked, C_m-spec requires more than one wh-specifier.

doc_id=94.tetml page=56 block_id=56-6 bbox=67.4,437.1,542.9,563.6 1203 1208
line=1203  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :Alternatively, D-linked multiple questions might be formed (and receive normal "pair-list" readings) with the
line=1204  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3 :complementizer otherwise reserved for non-multiple questions — the interrogative complementizer C_1-spec
line=1205  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :that takes only one wh-phrase as specifier. On this view, we would not need the exception clause built into
line=1206  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :(79), but we would need to understand why the semantics of D-linked multiple questions allows a
line=1207  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :complementizer that is otherwise not found in such questions. I do not know at present how to decide
line=1208  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:between the two hypotheses.46

doc_id=94.tetml page=56 block_id=56-7 bbox=67.4,73.5,545.5,403.6 1209 1223
line=1209  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       More generally, it remains unclear why D-linked phrases should constitute an exception to the
line=1210  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :Multiple-Specifier requirement. In this domain, the present proposal leaves an important question
line=1211  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :unanswered. This is not grounds for giving up on the proposal, however. Even when one is forced to leave
line=1212  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :some aspect of a phenomenon unexplained, one can often tell whether the discussion is on the right track by
line=1213  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :examining whether the unexplained portion of the phenomenon has internal coherence. If so, there are
line=1214  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :grounds for optimism about the overall approach — grounds for suspecting that the unanswered question is
line=1215  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :a real question about the true theory, and not merely an artifact of missteps and false notions. In the present
line=1216  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:case, if the absence of Superiority Effects with D-linked wh in English is due to an exception to the Multiple-
line=1217  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :Specifier requirement, we immediately expect this exception to show up in a slightly different way in
line=1218  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :Bulgarian. In English, the Multiple-Specifier requirement, combined with the pronunciation principles we
line=1219  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :stated earlier, produces one overt occurrence of wh-phrase movement, and one covert occurrence. In
line=1220  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :Bulgarian, the Multiple-Specifier requirement, combined with the pronunciation principles for that language,
line=1221  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:forces the overt fronting of at least two wh-phrases. Consequently, if the D-linking exception to English
line=1222  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :Superiority effects arises from an exception to the Multiple-Specifier requirement, we expect D-linking to
line=1223  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :improve Bulgarian multiple questions in which just one wh-phrase has fronted. As already mentioned in

doc_id=94.tetml page=58 block_id=58-4 bbox=67.4,531.0,537.2,680.8 1241 1247
line=1241  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       As it happens, Pesetsky (1987) (citing Wachowicz (1974) and Choe, personal communication)
line=1242  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:already presented the Polish counterpart of the previous section's Bulgarian facts as an argument for the
line=1243  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:hypothesis that D-linked wh-in-situ may fail to undergo covert phrasal wh-movement.  The way that paper
line=1244  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:saw things, questions with D-linking were not an exception to a Multiple-Specifier requirement, but rather
line=1245  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:were an exception to a proposed requirement that each wh-phrase undergo some form of phrasal whmovement
line=1246  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:          by LF. Polish was seen as a language that "wears its LF on its sleeve", thanks to the
line=1247  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:phenomenon of multiple overt wh-phrase movement. The discussion had certain marked deficiencies,

doc_id=94.tetml page=58 block_id=58-5 bbox=67.4,412.9,545.6,518.0 1248 1252
line=1248  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :however. For its conclusions to have force, it was necessary to assume that Polish wh-movement is always
line=1249  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :overt (an assumption not made explicit in Pesetsky 1987). Furthermore (needless to say) the possibility of
line=1250  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :feature movement was not considered at all.  In this context, it was reasonable to assume that D-linking is an
line=1251  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :exception to a movement requirement for wh-phrases, rather than an exception to a requirement on the
line=1252  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:specifiers of C_m-spec.

doc_id=94.tetml page=58 block_id=58-6 bbox=67.4,343.2,541.9,379.4 1253 1254
line=1253  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :       In fact, however, evidence now available to us favors the latter view over the former. Recall that the
line=1254  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:Multiple-Specifier requirement is satisfied once two wh-phrases have moved to SPEC of C_m-spec.

doc_id=94.tetml page=58 block_id=58-7 bbox=67.4,319.0,540.8,330.1 1255 1255
line=1255  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:Superiority effects arise in binary questions without D-linking because such questions contain only two whphrases

doc_id=94.tetml page=58 block_id=58-8 bbox=67.4,248.3,542.7,306.0 1256 1258
line=1256  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :        in the first place. Consequently, a derivation in which one of the two wh-phrases undergoes feature
line=1257  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :movement inevitably violates the Multiple-Specifier requirement. The situation should be different,
line=1258  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:however, in multiple questions that contain more than two wh-phrases. In such a question, nothing said so

doc_id=94.tetml page=58 block_id=58-9 bbox=67.4,224.1,535.3,235.3 1259 1259
line=1259  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:far should block a derivation in which one or more of the wh-phrases undergoes wh-feature movement, so

doc_id=94.tetml page=58 block_id=58-10 bbox=67.4,199.9,532.5,211.1 1260 1260
line=1260  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:long as at least two wh-phrases undergo the phrasal version of wh-movement. In particular, in a question

doc_id=94.tetml page=58 block_id=58-11 bbox=67.4,175.8,504.7,186.9 1261 1261
line=1261  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:with three or more wh-phrases, wh1 (the highest wh-phrase) should be able to undergo wh-feature

doc_id=94.tetml page=58 block_id=58-12 bbox=67.4,103.2,532.5,160.9 1262 1264
line=1262  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :movement as the first instance of wh-movement (satisfying AC), with two of the lower wh-phrases
line=1263  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :undergoing phrasal movement. Of these instances of phrasal movement, the first will be overt in English,
line=1264  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:and the rest will be covert. In other words, independent of D-linking, questions with three or more wh-

line=1273  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:and what second. By the pronunciation principles, movement of who should be the overt instance of
line=1274  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :movement. Since this not the case in (82a), the sentence is deviant. Example (82b), on the other hand,

line=1278  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:overt, and the result is (82b).

doc_id=94.tetml page=59 block_id=59-10 bbox=67.4,320.8,537.1,355.2 1279 1280
line=1279  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       The disappearance of Superiority effects with non-binary multiple questions makes it clear that the

doc_id=94.tetml page=59 block_id=59-11 bbox=67.4,205.5,541.4,307.8 1281 1285
line=1281  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:        undergo phrasal wh-movement. This, in turn, tells us exactly which property of grammar D-linked
line=1282  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:questions are exceptions to. Despite our ignorance concerning the semantic source of this D-linking
line=1283  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:exception, the strong hidden parallels between Bulgarian and English revealed by this approach suggest that
line=1284  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:we are on the right track.  The failure of D-linked questions to display the Superiority Effect in English
line=1285  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:groups with the fact that D-linking in Bulgarian obviates the requirement that two wh-phrases move overtly.

doc_id=94.tetml page=61 block_id=61-7 bbox=67.4,346.9,537.3,381.3 1325 1326
line=1325  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       One final empirical point must be investigated. The proposal in this section has presupposed that
line=1326  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:wh1-in-situ in non-D-linked ternary questions has essentially the same syntax as its counterpart in D-linked

doc_id=94.tetml page=61 block_id=61-8 bbox=67.4,252.0,541.8,332.0 1327 1330
line=1327  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:binary questions. That is, it fails to undergo phrasal wh-movement — but it does undergo wh-feature
line=1328  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:movement, if our hypothesis is correct. ACD evidence bearing on this point is hard to come by. In order to
line=1329  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:construct a fair test, we need to avoid D-linking, and we need at least four argument places to work with (in
line=1330  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:order to vary the status of the wh-phrase with ACD from wh1-in-situ to wh2-in-situ while holding other

doc_id=94.tetml page=61 block_id=61-9 bbox=67.4,135.8,545.7,238.1 1331 1335
line=1331  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :conditions constant). To the extent that such examples can be constructed, and to the extent that they do not
line=1332  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :pose insuperable burdens on linguistic memory, the facts appear to be as expected. It is exceedingly difficult

line=1342  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:the existence of wh-feature movement. This was the observation that if wh-feature movement can be the

line=1351  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:wh1 would be free to remain overlooked by wh-attraction. The Multiple Specifier Requirement would filter

doc_id=94.tetml page=66 block_id=66-17 bbox=67.4,90.2,545.6,147.9 1442 1444
line=1442  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:fact, in essence, as the free choice of which wh-phrase moves second in Bulgarian overt phrasal movement.
line=1443  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :(In addition, (84a-b) has already displayed examples in Bulgarian of the derivation now being considered in
line=1444  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :English — examples in which the first instance of wh-movement is feature movement in a Bulgarian multiple

doc_id=94.tetml page=67 block_id=67-1 bbox=0,0,0,0 0 0

doc_id=94.tetml page=67 block_id=67-2 bbox=313.9,749.6,332.5,760.7 1445 1445
line=1445  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:-67-

doc_id=94.tetml page=67 block_id=67-3 bbox=67.4,647.3,536.4,727.2 1446 1449
line=1446  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :question.) We thus have support for the hypothesis that in apparent Superiority violations in English, the
line=1447  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :first instance of wh-movement is actually feature movement — specifically, feature movement that satisfies
line=1448  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:AC.56 Thus, apparent exceptions to the Superiority Effect, when examined more closely, are really no
line=1449  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :exceptions at all.

doc_id=94.tetml page=67 block_id=67-4 bbox=67.4,306.9,545.6,613.8 1450 1463
line=1450  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       This evidence also bears on an issue that we have not discussed so far. We set for ourselves the
line=1451  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :problem of explaining apparent violations of AC. Our proposal has the interesting consequence that these
line=1452  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :violations are merely apparent. AC is being satisfied by an instance of wh-movement that had not previously
line=1453  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :been postulated. (The alternative involving "invisibility" also had this property.) We might have chosen to
line=1454  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :consider another possibility: that apparent violations of AC really do violate this constraint.  One approach
line=1455  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:of this kind might use the logic of Optimality Theory (Prince and Smolensky 1993) in which certain
line=1456  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :constraints on linguistic form can be violated when this is the only way to satisfy other, more highly valued
line=1457  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :(highly ranked) constraints. If the apparent Superiority violations discussed here were actual violations of
line=1458  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :AC, one would not expect to discover the evidence we have uncovered that these violations are merely
line=1459  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51 :apparent.57 In particular, one would be surprised to see AC violated in ternary questions, with no apparent
line=1460  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :pressure on output forms to minimize this violation by preferring overt movement of the second closest whphrase
line=1461  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       in cases where the first closest cannot (for some reason) move. Consequently, this set of apparent
line=1462  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :violations does not provide support for the view that constraints on movement are ranked and violable in an
line=1463  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :OT fashion.

doc_id=94.tetml page=67 block_id=67-5 bbox=67.4,83.7,544.7,273.4 1464 1472
line=1464  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :       This observation is of interest, since proposals that tend in the opposite direction (for different sets of
line=1465  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :data) have been advanced in a number of recent studies, including Grimshaw (1997) and many papers in
line=1466  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :Barbosa et al. (1998). In Pesetsky (1997; 1998), I suggested that those OT interactions that are visible in
line=1467  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :syntactic phenomena actually reflect the way in which phonology interprets syntax (e.g. via the
line=1468  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :pronunciation principles discussed above), and speculated that principles governing movement might not be
line=1469  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :ranked and violable in an OT fashion. The proposal about apparent Superiority violations presented here
line=1470  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:removes a case that might have seemed to support the opposing view.58 As far as we can tell, except for the
line=1471  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :effects of the PMC, AC is inviolable. In addition, we can draw a methodological moral: exceptions and
line=1472  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:violations are not necessarily what they appear to be. More takes place in syntax than meets the ear.59

doc_id=94.tetml page=70 block_id=70-9 bbox=67.4,407.3,542.8,507.8 1521 1525
line=1521  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       The next two sections take up (inconclusively) some loose ends left untied. In particular, we need to
line=1522  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:examine a few possible competitors to the hypothesis of "feature movement", to note their advantages and
line=1523  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:disadvantages – but, in the end, to show that our overall story is compatible with a variety of hypothesis
line=1524  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:concerning the true nature of what we have been calling "feature movement". We then move on to a deeper
line=1525  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:discussion of the specifier potential of interrogative complementizers.

doc_id=94.tetml page=70 block_id=70-10 bbox=84.2,339.4,347.1,350.6 1526 1526
line=1526  tag=O fonts=F0-11.16,F4-11.16:4.6.Is "feature movement" really feature movement?

doc_id=94.tetml page=70 block_id=70-11 bbox=67.4,106.0,541.9,305.0 1527 1535
line=1527  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :       One possible competitor to the "feature movement" hypothesis is relevant to an issue left open in the
line=1528  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :discussion so far: the choice between phrasal and feature movement in a derivation. Consider what happens
line=1529  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3         :when C_m-spec has been introduced into a structure and proceeds to attract instances of the wh-feature to it. I
line=1530  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :have suggested that this attraction may proceed in either of two ways: either the feature itself is attracted
line=1531  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :from an expression that bears it, or else the largest phrase that bears the feature is copied as a specifier of
line=1532  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16,F2-9.3:C_m-spec. We have also seen that certain properties of the attractor — i.e. properties external to the laws of
line=1533  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :movement — dictate which type of attraction occurs in particular cases. External properties include the fact
line=1534  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3         :that C_m-spec requires two specifiers and the fact that C_1-spec requires one, facts that we will explore in
line=1535  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :greater detail in the next section.

doc_id=94.tetml page=71 block_id=71-1 bbox=0,0,0,0 0 0

doc_id=94.tetml page=71 block_id=71-2 bbox=313.9,749.6,332.5,760.7 1536 1536
line=1536  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:-71-

doc_id=94.tetml page=71 block_id=71-3 bbox=67.4,513.4,542.8,727.2 1537 1546
line=1537  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       Are there other, more general preferences for one type of movement over the other, rooted in the
line=1538  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :laws of movement, in addition to "external" filters that may require phrasal movement in certain
line=1539  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :circumstances? As we noted earlier, Chomsky (1995, chapter 4) answered this question in the affirmative.
line=1540  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:He suggested that attraction of the smallest possible unit — the feature itself — is a more economical
line=1541  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :operation than attraction of any larger unit. The basis for Chomsky's particular claim was the idea that
line=1542  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :feature movement is the proper reanalysis of covert phrasal movement — coupled with the claim (inherited
line=1543  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :from earlier work) that covert movement is the default. Our discussion throughout this study has argued
line=1544  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :against the first of these claims. As noted earlier, it is not clear whether there is any particular reason to hold
line=1545  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :to the second of the claims, though it can certainly be modified so as to be consistent with our discussion in
line=1546  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :this study.

line=1549  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:introduction as a subconstituent of these words and phrases. In the case of an English wh-word, it is not

doc_id=94.tetml page=73 block_id=73-6 bbox=67.4,357.1,545.6,546.8 1599 1607
line=1599  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :Phrasal movement can now be seen as the copying of the closest bearer of the relevant feature. feature
line=1600  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :movement, by contrast, can now be seen as copying the smallest bearer of a feature. As suggested by
line=1601  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :Norvin Richards in unpublished work, and as mentioned earlier in this study, both conditions fit the spirit of
line=1602  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :"economy". Either is a plausible candidate for a genuine principle of grammar. Quite possibly, movement is
line=1603  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:possible if it meets either of these two criteria.66 Putting the matter in procedural terms, the target scans
line=1604  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :down the tree for the closest occurrence of the feature it attracts. When it finds an occurrence on a
line=1605  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :constituent, it has a choice: it either copies that constituent or else copies the smallest subconstituent that
line=1606  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :contains the feature. Excluded is copying of an intermediate constituent that bears the relevant feature, since
line=1607  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :it is neither the closest nor the smallest expression of the relevant feature.

doc_id=94.tetml page=73 block_id=73-7 bbox=67.4,87.4,542.8,323.6 1608 1618
line=1608  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       It is entirely possible, of course, that we will learn of other considerations that restrict the choice
line=1609  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:between feature (morpheme) movement and phrasal movement. For example, feature-movement for case
line=1610  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:purposes may be intrinsically preferred over phrasal movement. We were able to demonstrate the properties
line=1611  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:of feature movement successfully with the there-construction in part because (evidently) covert phrasal
line=1612  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:movement to T is impossible in this construction. In our discussion of ACD in multiple questions, we
line=1613  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:learned that covert phrasal movement to an VP-external object Case position is impossible. (Overt phrasal
line=1614  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:movement to subject position is the consequence of other considerations, often grouped under the rubric
line=1615  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:"Extended Projection Principle".) Conceivably, these two observations teach us that preferences for feature
line=1616  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:movement over phrasal movement exist. The question before us would be whether this preference is limited
line=1617  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:to movement for case purposes, or whether the preference is more general, in the spirit of Chomsky's
line=1618  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:(1995, chapter. 4) proposals. For now, I take these to be open questions.

doc_id=94.tetml page=75 block_id=75-10 bbox=67.4,102.3,545.6,292.0 1655 1663
line=1655  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       Another possibility is suggested by the research of Ochi (1998), who develops earlier ideas by
line=1656  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:Takahashi (1994). Recall from section 1.1 that Chomsky (1995, chapter 4) decomposed phrasal movement
line=1657  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:into two distinct operations: Attract F (feature attraction) and "generalized pied piping" (which forces the
line=1658  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:copying of phrasal material). Ochi (1998) argues that it is the "generalized pied piping" component of
line=1659  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:phrasal movement that is responsible for many of the island effects often grouped under the rubric of the
line=1660  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:Subjacency Condition. He suggests that these island effects arise from a conflict between a requirement that
line=1661  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:generalized pied piping copy a phrase to the closest possible landing site and other, conflicting requirements
line=1662  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:that prevent movement from targeting these very positions. As Ochi points out, this proposal entails that pure
line=1663  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:feature movement should not show these island effects at all — to which we may now add that pure feature

doc_id=94.tetml page=76 block_id=76-4 bbox=67.4,446.4,544.6,660.3 1667 1676
line=1667  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       As a final possibility, we might take the contrast between (94) and (95)-(97) as a sign of an deeper
line=1668  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :inaccuracy in the picture we have painted so far. Phrasal movement obeys both AC and subjacency, while
line=1669  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :what we have called "feature movement" obeys only AC. The fact that phrasal movement obeys a superset
line=1670  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :of the conditions on "feature movement" might be telling us that what we have been calling "feature
line=1671  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :movement", though it might be a subcomponent of movement, is something quite different from the
line=1672  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :operations traditionally called "movement". This is, in fact, the proposal advanced by Chomsky (1998). He
line=1673  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :suggests that phenomena that he previous identified (Chomsky 1995) as instances of feature movement are
line=1674  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:actually the result of a simpler operation called Agree. Agree merely establishes a link between an attracting
line=1675  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :head and the features that it seeks, without the copying operation characteristic of movement. Movement
line=1676  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51 :itself is simply Agree plus this copying.68

doc_id=94.tetml page=77 block_id=77-5 bbox=67.4,413.8,534.5,498.5 1697 1700

line=1700  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:English. The argument that the multiple-specifier requirement is not a deus ex machine came from

doc_id=94.tetml page=77 block_id=77-6 bbox=67.4,318.1,541.9,400.8 1701 1704
line=1701  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :Bulgarian, where failure to move at least two wh-phrases in a multiple question produces sharp
line=1702  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :unacceptability (except in a D-linked environment), which contrasts with mild deviance produced when
line=1703  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :additional wh-phrases are not fronted. Still, it would be useful to have converging evidence that the number
line=1704  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:of specifiers associated with C_m-spec is relevant to the detection of a Superiority Effect.

doc_id=94.tetml page=77 block_id=77-7 bbox=67.4,91.1,543.6,284.6 1705 1713
line=1705  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       This section provides converging evidence of just this sort, and in the process sheds light on other
line=1706  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:aspects of our story. In particular, we will tie a loose end from the opening sections of this study. In
line=1707  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:section 1.3, we saw three situations in which an otherwise expected Superiority Effect is not found. Two of
line=1708  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:these situations have been dealt with: English multiple questions with D-linking and multiple questions with
line=1709  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:more than two wh-phrases. The third case has not been discussed yet. This is the case of German, where,
line=1710  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:as we saw in example (34), even binary questions fail to display a Superiority Effect. We will turn to
line=1711  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:German after discussing some additional data from English.  More interesting still is the fact that English
line=1712  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:and German will turn out to fit into a simple typology of wh-specifier interactions — of which Japanese will
line=1713  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:exemplify the one language type undiscussed so far. This will be the topic of the final section of this study.

doc_id=94.tetml page=78 block_id=78-4 bbox=84.2,625.9,363.0,637.0 1718 1718

doc_id=94.tetml page=78 block_id=78-5 bbox=67.4,557.1,529.8,591.5 1719 1720
line=1719  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       In the previous section, we examined several apparent exceptions to the Superiority Effect —
line=1720  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:acceptable multiple questions with wh1-in-situ. The impossibility of ACD in wh1 taught us at a minimum

doc_id=94.tetml page=78 block_id=78-6 bbox=67.4,531.0,539.9,542.2 1721 1721
line=1721  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:that there is something special about wh1 in such cases. A phenomenon first noted in unpublished work by

doc_id=94.tetml page=78 block_id=78-7 bbox=67.4,505.0,488.8,516.1 1722 1722
line=1722  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:Kiss (1986) shows another property of wh1-in-situ that teaches us a similar lesson. In apparent

doc_id=94.tetml page=78 block_id=78-8 bbox=67.4,386.9,536.3,491.0 1723 1727
line=1723  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :counterexamples to the Superiority Effect, something special happens when a scope taking element such as
line=1724  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16,F2-9.3:negation intervenes between wh1 and the C_m-spec with which it is associated. For many speakers, at least
line=1725  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :as a first reaction, such examples are completely unacceptable. For other speakers (and perhaps for all
line=1726  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :speakers when the possibility is pointed out to them), the examples are acceptable so long as they receive a
line=1727  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                :"single pair" rather than a pair-list reading.

doc_id=94.tetml page=78 block_id=78-9 bbox=67.4,319.0,539.1,353.4 1728 1729
line=1728  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       A representative paradigm is displayed in (98). Examples (98a) and (98b) are experimental controls
line=1729  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:— normal multiple questions in which wh1 has undergone overt phrasal movement. Nothing special

doc_id=94.tetml page=78 block_id=78-10 bbox=67.4,291.1,533.4,304.1 1730 1730
line=1730  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:happens when negation intervenes between C_m-spec and wh2-in-situ in such cases. Example (98c) shows

doc_id=94.tetml page=78 block_id=78-11 bbox=67.4,266.9,508.2,278.1 1731 1731
line=1731  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:wh1-in-situ (i.e. an apparent Superiority violation). Here, if we are correct, the first instance of whmovement

line=1735  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3         :the clitic form of negation moves to C_m-spec with the auxiliary verb. As a consequence of this movement,
line=1736  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16,F2-9.3:negation intervenes between wh1 and C_m-spec . Example (98d) does produce special judgments:

line=1739  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16                  :       a. Which person __ did not read which book?

doc_id=94.tetml page=79 block_id=79-4 bbox=67.4,372.9,544.6,564.5 1744 1752
line=1744  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :Though, as the asterisk indicates, many speakers regard (98d) as completely unacceptable, the marginal
line=1745  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :acceptability of the single-pair reading in this and similar examples will be noted by superscripting and
line=1746  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :underscoring the judgment indication. The single-pair reading for (98d) is one in which it asks for the name
line=1747  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :of a single person and a single book, such that the person did not read the book. For example, suppose you
line=1748  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :pass a classroom and hear the teacher yelling. You know that this teacher only yells at his class when a
line=1749  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :student has failed to read his book for that day. In such a context (and only in this type of context), some
line=1750  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:speakers will accept a question like Which book didn't which person read today? For the time being, I will
line=1751  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :put aside the single-pair readings of examples like these, and confine my presentation of judgments on
line=1752  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :multiple questions to the pair-list reading.

doc_id=94.tetml page=93 block_id=93-10 bbox=67.4,93.0,541.9,238.1 2052 2058
line=2052  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :       If the Intervention Effect diagnoses the presence of "restriction material" stranded within an
line=2053  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :interrogative clause, it can be used as a probe to discover instances of feature movement in languages and
line=2054  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :constructions where our previous test, ACD, is unavailable. German, for example, lacks VP-ellipsis and
line=2055  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:seems to lack other instances of anaphora with the right set of properties.83 If we use the Intervention Effect
line=2056  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :as a probe for feature movement in German multiple questions, we discover a notable difference between
line=2057  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :English and German. I will argue that a partial explanation for this difference is available to us, and that this
line=2058  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :explanation in turn supports the overall architecture of our story.

line=2230  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:       I take these examples to show that German generally lacks the Superiority Effect.91 This is an
line=2231  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :interesting result, since it is not otherwise obvious (independent of our proposals) why German should
line=2232  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :show greater freedom than English with respect to Superiority, but less freedom than English with respect to
line=2233  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:the Intervention Effect. Our proposals link these two facts.92

doc_id=94.tetml page=101 block_id=101-7 bbox=67.4,260.4,544.6,340.4 2234 2237
line=2234  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       Before proceeding further, I need to note that the status of Superiority Effects in German is rather
line=2235  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:controversial. A number of investigators, including Büring (1994) and Fanselow (1991; 1997) have pointed
line=2236  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:out that long-distance wh-movement shows contrasts that look like a Superiority effect. The examples in

doc_id=94.tetml page=102 block_id=102-5 bbox=67.4,375.7,545.6,524.5 2246 2252
line=2246  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:One way of explaining the contrast in (147), considered by Fanselow, relies on the idea that the Superiority
line=2247  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:Effect is active in German in just the same fashion as it is in English — i.e. the opposite of what we have
line=2248  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:concluded here. What allows apparent violations of Superiority in German, in this proposal, is the
line=2249  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:possibility of scrambling. In a multiple question in which the object undergoes overt wh-movement, while
line=2250  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:the subject remains in-situ, the object (on this view) first scrambles to a position higher than the subject. The
line=2251  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:object is now structurally higher than the subject, and consequently not only can but must be the first whelement
line=2252  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:        attracted by the interrogative complementizer:

line=2275  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       This is an attractive competitor to our proposal, since (like our proposal) it reduces the difference in
line=2276  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:Superiority Effects between German and English to an independent difference: here, the availability of
line=2277  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:scrambling in German and its unavailability in English. There is an alternative explanation for the contrast in
line=2278  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:(147), however, which does not rely on facts about scrambling. Example (147b) shows an instance of overt
line=2279  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:wh-movement from an embedded finite clause, while (147a) does not. As it happens, many speakers reject

doc_id=94.tetml page=104 block_id=104-4 bbox=67.4,555.2,522.2,612.9 2280 2282
line=2280  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :wh-movement from embedded finite clauses altogether. Even the many speakers who do not reject whmovement
line=2281  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :          from embedded finite clauses find such examples more difficult to accept than more local
line=2282  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:instances of wh-movement. This factor alone could explain the contrast between (147a) and (147b).93

doc_id=94.tetml page=104 block_id=104-5 bbox=67.4,439.9,530.7,519.9 2283 2286
line=2283  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       Still, if a wh-phrase may scramble before undergoing wh-movement, and if this scrambling
line=2284  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :operation allows objects to count as closest to the complementizer than subjects, we do have a source for
line=2285  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :apparent Superiority violations independent of the hypotheses presented here. Indeed, it is not established
line=2286  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:that scrambling to the left of the subject can feed overt wh-movement in the manner assumed in the

doc_id=94.tetml page=104 block_id=104-6 bbox=67.4,415.7,515.8,426.9 2287 2287

line=2288  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:phrase does not undergo subsequent overt phrasal wh-movement, as noted by several researchers. Fanselow

doc_id=94.tetml page=104 block_id=104-8 bbox=67.4,367.3,523.3,378.5 2289 2289
line=2289  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:(1990), for example, observed that while scrambling of a non-wh-phrase is acceptable inside a multiple

doc_id=94.tetml page=104 block_id=104-9 bbox=67.4,252.9,540.0,354.3 2290 2294
line=2290  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :question (as seen in (150)), scrambling of the wh-phrase that does not undergo overt phrasal wh-movement
line=2291  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :is impossible (as seen in (150)). (This generalization is due to Engel 1972, according to Sauerland 1998b;
line=2292  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :see also Müller and Sternefeld 1996, 483.) Example (150) shows that Superiority is not what is at stake in
line=2293  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :(150), while (150) is the variant of (150) without scrambling. Examples (151) provides a similar paradigm

doc_id=94.tetml page=111 block_id=111-11 bbox=84.2,211.1,310.7,222.3 2435 2435
line=2435  tag=O fonts=F0-11.16:5.5.Japanese and a typology of wh-specifiers

doc_id=94.tetml page=111 block_id=111-12 bbox=67.4,76.3,543.7,176.7 2436 2440
line=2436  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       The earlier parts of this section provided support for a key component of our account of apparent
line=2437  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:superiority violations: the notion of "specifier potential". According to our proposal, the German lexicon
line=2438  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:contains only C1-spec, while the English (and Bulgarian) lexicon contains both C1-spec and Cm-spec. This
line=2439  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:lexical difference, I argued, is the key to gross differences in the distribution of the Intervention Effect in
line=2440  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:German and English multiple questions. Since German allows only one wh-specifier per question, the

doc_id=94.tetml page=112 block_id=112-1 bbox=0,0,0,0 0 0

doc_id=94.tetml page=112 block_id=112-2 bbox=311.1,749.6,335.3,760.7 2441 2441
line=2441  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:-112-

doc_id=94.tetml page=112 block_id=112-3 bbox=67.4,626.8,544.7,727.2 2442 2446
line=2442  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:restrictions of the other wh-phrases in a multiple question remain separated from the interrogative
line=2443  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:complementizer. This generates an Intervention Effect when a scope-bearing element occupies an intervening
line=2444  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:position. Since English allows multiple wh-specifiers, the Intervention Effect is found only in cases where
line=2445  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:an apparent violation of Superiority indicates that feature-movement has taken place from a wh-phrase in
line=2446  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:situ.

doc_id=94.tetml page=112 block_id=112-4 bbox=67.4,448.2,537.2,593.3 2447 2453
line=2447  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       Alongside interrogative complementizers that require multiple specifiers and interrogative
line=2448  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:complementizers that require a single specifier, it is reasonable to expect to find an interrogative
line=2449  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:complementizer that tolerates no specifiers whatsoever: i.e. C0-spec. As it happens, our hypotheses make
line=2450  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:very specific predictions about the properties questions introduced by C0-spec..  I will argue that C0-spec
line=2451  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:does exist, and that these predictions seem to be fully confirmed. In particular, I will suggest that Japanese
line=2452  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:(and Korean) wh-questions are introduced by C0-spec. Japanese/Korean, German and English/Bulgarian
line=2453  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:thus round out the paradigm of "specifier potential" for interrogative complementizers:

doc_id=94.tetml page=113 block_id=113-7 bbox=67.4,478.9,542.0,538.5 2470 2472
line=2470  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :       Except for differences in specifier potential, the interrogative complementizer used for wh-questions
line=2471  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :should be fundamentally identical across languages. Consequently, we expect that Japanese and Korean
line=2472  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:C_0-spec, like C_1-spec and C_m-spec, bears an uninterpretable wh-feature. If this feature is not deleted in the

doc_id=94.tetml page=113 block_id=113-8 bbox=67.4,452.9,543.7,465.9 2473 2473
line=2473  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:course of the derivation, the derivation should crash. Since C_0-spec does not allow wh-phrase movement to

doc_id=94.tetml page=113 block_id=113-9 bbox=67.4,428.7,542.8,439.9 2474 2474
line=2474  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:form a specifier, only wh-feature movement (or its counterpart in the variant proposals discussed above) can

doc_id=94.tetml page=113 block_id=113-10 bbox=67.4,402.7,524.2,415.7 2475 2475
line=2475  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:delete the uninterpretable feature on C_0-spec. Consequently, a wh-question in such a language — be it a

doc_id=94.tetml page=113 block_id=113-11 bbox=67.4,376.6,539.9,389.7 2476 2476
line=2476  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16,F2-9.3:single question or a multiple question — must contain at least one wh-phrase not separated from C_0-spec by

doc_id=94.tetml page=113 block_id=113-12 bbox=67.4,304.1,541.8,363.6 2477 2479
line=2477  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :an intervening scope-bearer. If the question contains just one wh-phrase, and this wh-phrase is separated
line=2478  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:from C_0-spec by a scope-bearing intervener, the question should be unacceptable. As noted by Hoji (1985),
line=2479  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :this is indeed the case in Japanese. A scope-bearing element in a single-wh-question produces an

doc_id=94.tetml page=113 block_id=113-13 bbox=67.4,256.7,534.4,291.1 2480 2481
line=2480  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:Intervention Effect whenever it comes between the wh-phrase and the interrogative complementizer. As in
line=2481  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:German, scrambling eliminates the violation:

doc_id=94.tetml page=124 block_id=124-5 bbox=67.4,441.7,544.6,567.3 2679 2684
line=2679  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:       Some controversy surrounds these observations as well. For one thing, the sharp cases of the
line=2680  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:"English-style" Superiority Effect seem to involve situations like (181), in which one wh-phrase comes from
line=2681  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:a higher clause than the other. Other examples show weaker and more variable effects. If so, we might not
line=2682  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:be dealing with a Superiority Effect at all in (181), but with a simpler contrast between longer and shorterdistance
line=2683  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:        scrambling — much as I suggested for German examples like (147a-b). In support of this is the
line=2684  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:fact that multiple questions with left-peripheral wh-phrases do show an Intervention Effect when a scopebearing

doc_id=94.tetml page=124 block_id=124-6 bbox=67.4,230.6,541.8,428.7 2685 2693
line=2685  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :        element c-commands an unmoved wh-phrase in the question: a German pattern. If this is the case,
line=2686  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :then our picture of Japanese must be more complex than represented so far. We must actually allow
line=2687  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-9.3:Japanese questions to be introduced by C_0-spec, C_1-spec or C_m-spec: the first for in-situ questions, the
line=2688  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16       :second for questions like those in (181), and the third for "Bulgarian-style" questions like those in (180) —

line=2823  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:linked questions" or "questions with D-linking", even though technically it is wh-phrases that are D-linked.
line=2824  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:Any attempt to explain the semantic sources of the syntactic properties of D-linking will require more
line=2825  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:conclusive investigation of this issue.

line=2924  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:it.

line=2926  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:of the role of linguistic experience in language acquisition. This fact means that certain differences among
line=2927  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:languages are virtually guaranteed to be irreducible. It is certainly possible (though not inevitable) that this is

line=2971  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:         Perhaps the best argument I know in favor of this proposition is Wurmbrand's (1998) discussion
line=2972  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:of "restructuring" phenomena in German. She argues persuasively that infinitival complements to
line=2973  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:restructuring predicates are significantly smaller than CP or TP, and may be bare VPs. She then shows that
line=2974  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:although a bare VP complement to a restructuring predicate may contain a verb and its object, the licensing of
line=2975  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:object case does not take place within this domain, but instead depends on the case properties of the
line=2976  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:restructuring predicate. The link between the "smallness" of the embedded VP and the absence of object
line=2977  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:case licensing in that domain forms a good argument that object case licensing depends on VP-external
line=2978  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:structure.

line=3110  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :derivations whose patterns of wh-movement and non-movement match those of an "input" derivation. (In
line=3111  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :OT phonology, among the constraints governing pronunciation are some that favor "Faithfulness" to an
line=3112  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :input form - in just this fashion. Only constraints ranked higher than a given Faithfulness constraint can
line=3113  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :enforce a deviation from the input with respect to the property singled out by the Faithfulness constraint.)
line=3114  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-9.3 :M_OVEMENT F_AITHFULNESS strongly resembles the proposal of Legendre, Smolensky and Wilson (1998).

line=3205  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:       67 For the details of the relevant conditions, Ochi follows Takahashi (1994). He argues, for
line=3206  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :example, that adjunction to individual members of multi-member chains is forbidden by a general

doc_id=94.tetml page=147 block_id=147-3 bbox=67.4,411.1,545.5,716.1 3212 3225
line=3212  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :       On one key point, Ochi's hypotheses and ours are incompatible. Ochi follows Takahashi in arguing
line=3213  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :that the constraint on generalized pied piping that requires extremely local landing sites is "mover-oriented"
line=3214  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :rather than "attractor-oriented". He suggests, in fact, that the relevant constraint is Shortest Move. If this
line=3215  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:were the case, we would expect the PMC to never license violations of island conditions, for the same
line=3216  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :reason the PMC never licenses violations of the "tucking in" requirement (as discussed in the final paragraph
line=3217  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :of section 2.2).  There is no "tax relief" from tucking in because Shortest Move is not a constraint governing
line=3218  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :the distance between an Attractor and Attractee, but rather a constraint that chooses the exact position near a
line=3219  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :given Attractor to which copying takes place. There is, as we have seen, "tax relief" from island conditions.
line=3220  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :Consequently, the two phenomena cannot both be traced back to Shortest Move.

line=3359  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:         As already noted, one also wants to know why the Intervention Effect exists. Some considerations
line=3360  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:advanced by Reinhart (1998) suggest a possible line of attack, though some rethinking is necessary.
line=3361  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:According to Reinhart, Pesetsky (1986) proposed that all D-linked wh-in-situ are interpreted in situ, rather
line=3362  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:than by covert phrasal movement. She then proceeds to show that on the simplest assumptions about in-situ
line=3363  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:interpretation of wh-phrases, this suggestion fails. In particular, in a downward entailing environment, if

line=3381  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :On the one hand, Reinhart is not correct about the details of my (1986) proposal. In that paper, I argued that
line=3382  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:D-linked wh may (not "must") be interpreted in situ. Nonetheless, one wonders if — in those cases where

doc_id=94.tetml page=154 block_id=154-9 bbox=67.4,115.3,542.8,330.1 3383 3392
line=3383  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :the only parse for a multiple question involves wh-feature movement — the deviance attributed to the
line=3384  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :"Intervention Effect" might actually be attributable to the "Donald Duck" problem. It is necessary to imagine
line=3385  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :that questions which fail to control their answers are actually felt as deviant — which is, of course, the
line=3386  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :sticking point here. Nonetheless, if this conjecture is correct, Reinhart's observation may have (semiinadvertently
line=3387  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :             ) provided the key to understanding the Intervention Effect. That is, she may be right about the
line=3388  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :interpretive difficulties of in-situ restrictions, but wrong to suppose that this poses a problem. It might
line=3389  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :instead offer a solution to a problem: why the Intervention Effect holds. Unfortunately, this proposal does
line=3390  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:not cover cases of the Intervention Effect involving interveners like every, which are not downward
line=3391  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :entailing for their nuclear scope. If these cases are of a piece with the others, Reinhart's suggestion is not
line=3392  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :apropos here. Honcoop (1988) offers an alternative that might be investigated in its place.

doc_id=94.tetml page=160 block_id=160-9 bbox=67.4,139.5,544.6,311.5 3513 3520
line=3513  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:key" for the answer (Kuno 1982). Thus, a person who asks Which person bought which book? normally
line=3514  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :expects an answer that exhausts some domain of people, but not necessarily any domain of books, while the
line=3515  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:person who asks Which book did which person buy? normally has the opposite expectation. No such
line=3516  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :difference can be imagined in Wiltschko's cases, where the expected answer naturally exhausts the relevant
line=3517  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :set no matter what. Suppose it is the case that the requirement of a wh-specifier needs to be satisfied as early
line=3518  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :as possible in the derivation, except when delaying the requirement makes an interpretive difference. Such a
line=3519  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :condition on the patterns of movement might handle Wiltschko's observation, since the (b) examples, if we
line=3520  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :are correct, show feature movement preceding phrasal movement.

doc_id=94.tetml page=165 block_id=165-10 bbox=67.4,358.0,524.2,369.2 3620 3620
line=3620  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:If Japanese wh-in-situ always associate with interrogative C by wh-feature movement, one might expect

line=3621  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:them also to disobey subjacency and not to pay a "Subjacency Tax". This is true up to a point. Wh-phrases

line=3622  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :quite generally fail to show Complex Noun Phrase Constraint effects, but they do show wh-island effects,
line=3623  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16         :as documented by Watanabe (1992).. In addition, they do pay a "Subjacency Tax"(governed by the PMC)
line=3624  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F2-11.16:for wh-island violations, as Watanabe also documented. Wh-feature movement of dare-ni in (ii) to the

doc_id=94.tetml page=166 block_id=166-5 bbox=67.4,321.8,539.0,489.2 3636 3643
line=3636  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:It is not clear how we should understand the contradiction between (ia-b) and our observations concerning
line=3637  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:feature movement in English. It is possible that this contradiction reveals some fundamental problem with
line=3638  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:the hypotheses advanced here. It may also be the case that the contradiction simply reveals how the PMC
line=3639  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:individuates syntactic relations. In (i)b we observe (if our ideas about Japanese are correct) an instance of
line=3640  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:feature movement rescuing another instance of feature movement from subjacency effects. In (95)-(97), by
line=3641  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:contrast, we were examining cases in which an instance of feature movement might have been expected to
line=3642  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:rescue an instance phrasal movement. This might make a difference, but I will leave the question open for
line=3643  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:now.

doc_id=94.tetml page=166 block_id=166-6 bbox=67.4,74.4,545.6,243.7 3644 3651
line=3644  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:       104Beck (1996) and Beck and Kim (1996) suggest a different cross-linguistic predictor for the
line=3645  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :Intervention Effect. They note that both Korean and German (the languages that they discuss) allow
line=3646  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :scrambling to remove a wh-phrase from the scope of a potential intervener, while English does not. They
line=3647  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :suggest that if a language has a scrambling process that can eliminate an Intervention Effect, it must use it —
line=3648  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :and speculate that the absence of scrambling correlates with the absence of the Intervention Effect.  For
line=3649  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :them, the Intervention Effect is an island condition on traces of movement that have not been formed as early
line=3650  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :in the derivation as possible. It is thus restricts "LF traces" in a language like German or Korean where
line=3651  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :scrambling can yield an overt-syntax trace in the same environment, but remains silent about comparable "LF

doc_id=94.tetml page=167 block_id=167-1 bbox=0,0,0,0 0 0

doc_id=94.tetml page=167 block_id=167-2 bbox=311.1,749.6,335.3,760.7 3652 3652
line=3652  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:-167-

doc_id=94.tetml page=167 block_id=167-3 bbox=67.4,593.3,538.2,716.1 3653 3658
line=3653  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:traces" in a language like English, where no overt process can create the trace earlier in the derivation. (As
line=3654  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:Beck and Kim note, the logic here follows Pesetsky's 1989 "Earliness Principle"; cf. also Diesing 1992.)
line=3655  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:They do not note, however, the Intervention Effect with which we began our discussion: the English effect
line=3656  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:found in multiple questions that appear to violate AC. One can imagine variants of their approach that might
line=3657  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:accommodate the Intervention Effect in English, but none of these (I think) straightforwardly extends to the
line=3658  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16:other properties of these constructions discussed earlier.

doc_id=94.tetml page=167 block_id=167-4 bbox=67.4,526.4,515.8,559.9 3659 3660
line=3659  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:       105This issue was brought to my attention by Hisatsugu Kitahara. I am also grateful to him for
line=3660  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :discussing the issue with me at length.

line=3681  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16,F1-6.51:       110 It will be interesting to investigate similar typologies in other domains.  There are some intriguing
line=3682  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :possibilities. In work still in progress, Guerzoni (1999) investigates whether the licensing of negative
line=3683  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :polarity items (NPIs) in English and Italian is, like the licensing of wh-phrases, accomplished sometimes by
line=3684  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :(covert) phrasal movement to the licensor, and sometimes by feature movement. Suggestive evidence in
line=3685  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :favor of this hypothesis comes from the fact that long-distance licensing of an NPI over an intervener (such a
line=3686  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :closer instance of negation) obeys island conditions that other instances of licensing do not, as noted by
line=3687  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :Kurata (1991). For example, licensing of an NPI by the nearest negation (or other licenser) does not display
line=3688  tag=O fonts=F1-11.16        :any subject/non-subject asymmetry.
